## Benchmarking

### Issue #288: Define benchmark taxonomy and naming convention

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Benchmark Foundation
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** architecture, benchmarking, codex-ready, performance
- **Dependencies:** None

**Scope**

Define the benchmark families, naming conventions, result metadata, and required output formats for numerical, workflow, HPC, AI, and UX-adjacent performance benchmarks.

**Deliverables**

- Benchmark taxonomy document
- Benchmark result JSON schema draft
- Naming convention for benchmark IDs

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] A document under `src/rietveld_next/benchmarks/` or `docs/benchmarking/` defines benchmark families and naming rules.
- [ ] Benchmark IDs include workstream, kernel, backend, size, and variant.
- [ ] The taxonomy explicitly distinguishes microbenchmarks, integration benchmarks, scientific validation benchmarks, and end-to-end workflow benchmarks.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #289: Create benchmark result schema

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Benchmark Foundation
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** benchmarking, codex-ready, performance, schema
- **Dependencies:** #288

**Scope**

Create a machine-readable schema for benchmark outputs that supports runtime, memory, numerical checksum, backend, hardware, software environment, and reproducibility metadata.

**Deliverables**

- JSON Schema for benchmark results
- Example valid result files
- Schema validation test

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Schema validates at least one Rust-style result and one Python/JAX-style result.
- [ ] Schema includes wall time median/min/max, iterations, warmup count, backend, dtype, input size, checksum, and environment metadata.
- [ ] Invalid results fail schema validation in tests.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #290: Create benchmark runner CLI skeleton

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Benchmark Foundation
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** benchmarking, cli, codex-ready, performance
- **Dependencies:** #289

**Scope**

Implement a benchmark runner CLI under `src/rietveld_next/benchmarks/` that can discover and run selected benchmarks and emit JSON and Markdown summaries.

**Deliverables**

- CLI entry point
- JSON output writer
- Markdown summary writer
- Unit tests for argument parsing

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Command supports selecting benchmark family, size, backend, iterations, warmup, and output path.
- [ ] CLI creates output directories when needed.
- [ ] CLI exits successfully when optional backends are unavailable and emits a clear skipped status.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #291: Add deterministic synthetic profile dataset generator

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Benchmark Foundation
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** benchmarking, codex-ready, data, performance
- **Dependencies:** #290

**Scope**

Implement deterministic synthetic data generation for profile-evaluation benchmarks, including x arrays, peak positions, amplitudes, widths, and metadata.

**Deliverables**

- Synthetic dataset generator
- Small/medium/large presets
- Determinism tests

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Repeated generation with the same seed produces identical arrays and metadata.
- [ ] Presets include small, medium, and large sizes.
- [ ] Generator records all parameters needed to reproduce the dataset.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #292: Implement Rust Gaussian profile microbenchmark

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Numerical Benchmarks
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** benchmarking, codex-ready, diffraction, performance, rust
- **Dependencies:** #291

**Scope**

Implement the safe Rust Gaussian profile-sum benchmark kernel and timing harness for a simplified powder diffraction profile calculation.

**Deliverables**

- Rust Gaussian profile function
- Rust benchmark executable or test harness
- Benchmark JSON output

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Kernel validates input lengths.
- [ ] Kernel uses `f64` and avoids avoidable allocations inside the peak loop.
- [ ] Benchmark reports median, min, max, iterations, input sizes, dtype, and checksum.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #293: Implement JAX Gaussian profile microbenchmark

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Numerical Benchmarks
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** benchmarking, codex-ready, jax, performance, python
- **Dependencies:** #291

**Scope**

Implement the JAX Gaussian profile-sum benchmark with compile time separated from steady-state execution time.

**Deliverables**

- JAX Gaussian profile function
- JAX timing harness
- Benchmark JSON output

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] JAX function is JIT compiled.
- [ ] First-call compile time is reported separately from steady-state runtime.
- [ ] The benchmark uses `.block_until_ready()` before stopping timers.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #294: Compare Rust and JAX Gaussian profile outputs

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Numerical Benchmarks
- **Priority:** P0
- **Labels:** benchmarking, codex-ready, correctness, jax, performance, rust
- **Dependencies:** #292, #293

**Scope**

Add correctness comparison between Rust and JAX Gaussian profile outputs when both backends are available from the runner.

**Deliverables**

- Cross-backend comparison test
- Tolerance policy
- Checksum comparison

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Small benchmark outputs match within float64 tolerance when both backends use float64.
- [ ] Tolerance is relaxed and explicitly reported when JAX uses float32.
- [ ] Mismatches include maximum absolute and relative error in failure output.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #297: Add benchmark skip policy for optional dependencies

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Benchmark Foundation
- **Priority:** P1
- **Labels:** benchmarking, ci, codex-ready, performance
- **Dependencies:** #290

**Scope**

Define and implement skip behavior for optional benchmark dependencies such as JAX, GPU runtime, PyO3 bindings, Ray, Dask, or MPI.

**Deliverables**

- Skip policy document
- Skip status in JSON schema
- Tests for missing optional backend

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Unavailable optional backends produce `skipped` results with a reason.
- [ ] Normal CI can run without JAX, GPU, MPI, Ray, or Dask.
- [ ] Skip behavior is visible in Markdown summaries.
- [ ] All implementation source is placed under `src/`; no forbidden top-level implementation directories are created.
- [ ] Benchmark can be skipped or constrained in normal CI so expensive workloads do not run by default.
- [ ] Results are reproducible with fixed seeds, explicit dataset sizes, software versions, and hardware metadata where available.

### Issue #298: Implement pseudo-Voigt profile microbenchmark

- **Category:** Benchmarking
- **Phase:** Numerical Benchmarks
- **Priority:** P1
- **Labels:** benchmarking, codex-ready, diffraction, performance
- **Dependencies:** #292, #293

**Scope**

Add a pseudo-Voigt profile benchmark to better approximate common Rietveld profile workloads beyond Gaussian peaks.

**Deliverables**

- Pseudo-Voigt kernel benchmark
- Synthetic data preset
- Rust and/or JAX implementation depending on available backend

**Acceptance criteria**

- [ ] Benchmark supports at least small and medium sizes.
- [ ] Output includes checksum and runtime statistics.
- [ ] Documentation explains differences from the Gaussian proxy benchmark.
